# Part 9 — JSON Schema / Appendix

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

Version: 2.0
Status: Draft
Owner: Insynergy Inc.
Author: Ryoji Morii

---

# 9.0 Appendix Overview

Part 9 is the **normative schema appendix** of the Master Specification.

Parts 1 through 6 define *what* the platform does and *why*. They describe artifacts in prose, illustrate them with YAML fragments, and constrain them with invariants. Part 9 consolidates every serialized artifact those parts describe into a single, formal, machine-checkable contract expressed as **JSON Schema (draft 2020-12)**.

This part introduces no new behavior.

It adds no new artifact, field, or constraint that is not already established by an earlier part. Where Part 9 appears to add a rule, that rule is the formal restatement of an invariant, decision matrix, or acceptance criterion already recorded upstream, and the originating section is cited.

Part 9 is **authoritative for structure**. Where a prose fragment in Parts 1–6 and a schema in Part 9 disagree on the *shape* of an artifact — a field name, a type, a cardinality, an enumeration value — the schema in Part 9 governs, and the discrepancy is recorded as a defect against the originating section for reconciliation. Where they disagree on *meaning*, the originating section governs and the schema is corrected.

```text
Parts 1–6        →   meaning, behavior, rationale   (authoritative for intent)
Part 9           →   structure, type, constraint    (authoritative for shape)
```

Every schema in Part 9 is traceable to the section that owns the artifact it describes.

---

# 9.1 Schema Architecture & Conventions

# 9.1.1 Purpose & Scope of the Appendix

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the purpose, scope, and boundary of the JSON Schema appendix.

The appendix exists so that every artifact the platform produces or consumes can be validated mechanically, before it is trusted, at the boundary between the layer that produces it and the layer that consumes it.

A prose description of an artifact is sufficient for a human reader. It is insufficient for a validator. A validator requires a schema: an explicit, closed, typed contract that a document either satisfies or violates, with no interpretation in between.

Part 9 supplies that contract for every artifact in the pipeline.

The scope of the appendix is **every serialized artifact and every embedded object** defined across Parts 1 through 6, including:

* the external product contract (Part 1);
* the complete Story artifact set (Part 2);
* the screenplay artifact set (Part 3);
* the shot and storyboard artifact set (Part 4);
* the rendering input, output, and runtime artifacts (Part 5);
* the build, execution, configuration, and operational-state artifacts (Part 6).

The appendix also defines the **shared vocabulary** — identifiers, hashes, timestamps, envelopes, and enumerations — that these artifacts hold in common, so that a single definition is referenced everywhere rather than restated per artifact.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following principle.

> **A schema is a contract. A document is valid or it is rejected. There is no third outcome.**

Four commitments follow.

1. **Closed by default.** Every object schema sets `additionalProperties: false` unless an artifact is explicitly defined as extensible. An unexpected field is a defect, not a courtesy.
2. **Explicit over implicit.** Every constraint an earlier part states in prose — a cardinality, an enumeration, a required field, a referential rule — is expressed in the schema where it can be checked, not left to the reader.
3. **Referenced, never duplicated.** A shared type is defined once in the common `$defs` and referenced by `$ref` everywhere it is used. A change to a shared type changes it everywhere at once.
4. **Traceable.** Every schema records, in its `description` and in this appendix's registry, the section that owns the artifact it validates.

A schema that admits a document the owning section would reject is a defective schema, and a schema that rejects a document the owning section would accept is equally defective.

---

# Terminology

| Term | Definition |
| ---- | ---------- |
| Artifact | A serialized document produced by one layer and consumed by another |
| Embedded object | A structured object that appears inside an artifact but is not itself independently serialized |
| Schema | A JSON Schema (draft 2020-12) document that validates an artifact or object |
| Envelope | The common provenance fields every sealed artifact carries |
| Common `$defs` | The shared library of reusable type definitions referenced across schemas |
| `$id` | The canonical, stable identifier of a schema |
| Owning Section | The section of Parts 1–6 that defines the artifact a schema validates |
| Sealed | An artifact that has been approved or emitted and is therefore immutable |

---

# What the Appendix Is

The appendix is the platform's **single source of structural truth**.

| Attribute | Definition |
| --------- | ---------- |
| Category | Normative schema contract |
| Schema language | JSON Schema draft 2020-12 |
| Coverage | Every serialized artifact and embedded object in Parts 1–6 |
| Authority | Authoritative for artifact *shape*; subordinate to owning sections for *meaning* |
| Consumers | Producers, consumers, validators, quality gates, and the build orchestrator |
| Failure condition | A schema that accepts an invalid artifact or rejects a valid one |

---

# What the Appendix Is Not

The appendix is **not** an implementation, a serializer, or a behavioral specification.

| The Appendix Is | The Appendix Is Not |
| --------------- | ------------------- |
| A structural contract | A runtime engine |
| A validation reference | A serialization library |
| A restatement of upstream invariants | A source of new invariants |
| Authoritative for shape | Authoritative for meaning |

A schema does not decide *whether* an artifact should be produced, *when* it is produced, or *what it means*. It decides only whether a produced document is structurally well-formed. Semantic authority remains with the owning section.

---

# Scope Boundary

```text
Upstream (Owning Sections, Parts 1–6)
        │  define meaning, behavior, invariants
        ▼
[ Part 9 Schema Appendix ]  ← validates structure only
        │  every artifact conforms or is rejected
        ▼
Validators / Quality Gates / Orchestrator
```

The appendix begins where an artifact is serialized and ends where it is validated. It does not reach into narrative reasoning, rendering execution, or provider behavior. It governs the shape of the documents that cross layer boundaries, and nothing else.

---

# Appendix Invariants

* INV-9.1.1-1 — Every serialized artifact in Parts 1–6 has exactly one governing schema in Part 9.
* INV-9.1.1-2 — Part 9 introduces no artifact, field, or constraint absent from its owning section.
* INV-9.1.1-3 — Part 9 is authoritative for artifact structure; owning sections are authoritative for meaning.
* INV-9.1.1-4 — Every schema is traceable to an owning section.
* INV-9.1.1-5 — A shared type is defined once and referenced, never duplicated.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.1 is complete when:

* The purpose of the appendix as the platform's structural contract is defined.
* The scope is fixed as every serialized artifact and embedded object in Parts 1–6.
* The authority split — structure to Part 9, meaning to the owning sections — is established.
* The closed-by-default, explicit, referenced, and traceable commitments are stated.
* Appendix invariants are enumerated and enforceable.

---

# 9.1.2 Schema Conventions

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the conventions every schema in Part 9 obeys.

Uniform conventions are what make the appendix legible and composable. A reader who learns the conventions once can read any schema in the appendix without relearning its idioms. A validator configured once validates every artifact identically.

The conventions cover the schema dialect, identifier scheme, structural defaults, naming, typing, and the treatment of required and optional fields.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts one convention rule.

> **Every schema looks the same, so every schema reads the same.**

Convention is not decoration. A consistent `$id` scheme makes cross-references mechanical. A uniform `additionalProperties` policy makes closure predictable. A single naming convention makes field names guessable. The conventions exist to remove every avoidable degree of freedom from the appendix.

---

# Schema Dialect

Every schema declares the draft 2020-12 dialect.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema"
}
```

Draft 2020-12 is the sole dialect used across the appendix. No schema mixes dialects, and no schema omits the `$schema` declaration. Features specific to the dialect — `$defs`, `prefixItems`, `unevaluatedProperties` — are used where appropriate and are always interpreted under 2020-12 semantics.

---

# The `$id` Scheme

Every schema carries a stable, canonical `$id` under a single namespace.

```text
https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/<layer>/<artifact>.schema.json
```

* `cttp` is the platform short name (Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform).
* `v2.0` is the specification version this appendix belongs to.
* `<layer>` is the owning layer segment: `vision`, `story`, `screenplay`, `shot`, `render`, or `build`.
* `<artifact>` is the kebab-case artifact name, matching its serialized filename where one exists.

Example identifiers:

```text
https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/story/dramatic-premise.schema.json
https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/shot/shot-list.schema.json
https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/render/render-manifest.schema.json
```

The shared definitions live at a single well-known identifier.

```text
https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json
```

`$id` values are stable. A schema's `$id` is never reused for a different artifact and never changed within a specification version. A breaking change to an artifact's shape produces a new specification version, not a silent redefinition under the same `$id`.

---

# Referencing

Cross-schema references use `$ref` against a schema's `$id` and JSON-Pointer fragments into `$defs`.

```json
{ "$ref": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json#/$defs/ShotId" }
```

Within a single schema, local references use a bare fragment.

```json
{ "$ref": "#/$defs/SceneHeading" }
```

Every `$ref` in the appendix resolves. A dangling reference is a schema defect. Shared types are referenced from `common/defs.schema.json`; artifact-local helper types are defined in the artifact schema's own `$defs`.

---

# Structural Defaults

Every object schema in the appendix obeys the following defaults unless a section explicitly overrides them.

| Convention | Rule |
| ---------- | ---- |
| `type` | Every schema declares an explicit top-level `type`. |
| `additionalProperties` | `false` on every object, unless the artifact is declared extensible. |
| `required` | Every mandatory field is listed in `required`; optional fields are omitted from it. |
| `unevaluatedProperties` | `false` on objects composed with `allOf`/`$ref` to preserve closure. |
| Arrays | Declare `items`; declare `minItems`/`maxItems` where a cardinality is specified upstream. |
| Empty objects | An object that is a valid empty slot declares `"type": "object"` and permits `{}`. |

Closure is the default because the platform's artifacts are closed contracts. An unexpected property is a signal that a producer and a schema have diverged, and the appendix surfaces that divergence as a validation failure rather than absorbing it silently.

---

# Naming Conventions

Names follow a single, mechanical convention.

* **Field names** are `snake_case`, matching the serialized artifacts exactly (`shot_id`, `render_strategy`, `content_hash`).
* **`$defs` type names** are `PascalCase` (`ShotId`, `ContentHash`, `ArtifactEnvelope`).
* **Enumeration values** are recorded verbatim from the owning section, preserving case and underscores (`medium_close_up`, `runway_video`, `low_key`).
* **Filenames** in `$id` are kebab-case and match the artifact's serialized name (`shot-list`, `render-manifest`).

An enumeration value is never aliased, abbreviated, pluralized, or re-cased in the appendix. It is copied exactly from the section that defines it, consistent with Invariant P-445 (4.1.3).

---

# Required vs Optional

The appendix expresses the required/optional distinction exactly as the owning section states it.

* A field the owning section marks *required* appears in the schema's `required` array.
* A field the owning section marks *optional* is defined in `properties` but omitted from `required`.
* A field the owning section marks *conditional* is expressed with `if`/`then` or `dependentRequired`, with the condition traced to the section.

Where an owning section says "every field is mandatory" (for example the Shot Schema of 4.1.2), every property appears in `required`. Where an owning section annotates fields as optional (for example `character_refs` and `dependencies` in `shot-list.json`, 5.1.4), those fields are excluded from `required`.

---

# Convention Invariants

* INV-9.1.2-1 — Every schema declares the draft 2020-12 `$schema`.
* INV-9.1.2-2 — Every schema carries a stable `$id` under the `cttp/v2.0` namespace.
* INV-9.1.2-3 — Every object schema sets `additionalProperties: false` unless declared extensible.
* INV-9.1.2-4 — Every `$ref` resolves; dangling references are defects.
* INV-9.1.2-5 — Enumeration values are recorded verbatim from their owning section.
* INV-9.1.2-6 — The required/optional/conditional status of every field matches its owning section.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.2 is complete when:

* The sole schema dialect is fixed as JSON Schema draft 2020-12.
* The `$id` namespace scheme is defined and stable.
* Cross-schema and local referencing conventions are defined and always resolve.
* Structural defaults, including closed-by-default objects, are established.
* Naming conventions for fields, types, enumerations, and filenames are fixed.
* The required/optional/conditional treatment mirrors the owning sections.

---

# 9.1.3 Common Definitions & Shared Types

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the shared type library referenced by every schema in the appendix.

Many artifacts share the same primitive shapes: an identifier that matches a fixed pattern, a content hash, an ISO-8601 timestamp, a scene reference, a bounded score. Defining these once, in a single common schema, guarantees that a `shot_id` means exactly the same thing in the shot list, the camera plan, the blocking, the storyboard, the continuity report, and the render manifest.

The common definitions live at `common/defs.schema.json` and are referenced by `$ref` from every artifact schema.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **Define a type once. Reference it everywhere. Change it in one place.**

A `shot_id` pattern copied into twelve schemas will eventually be edited in eleven. A `shot_id` pattern defined once and referenced twelve times cannot drift. The common definitions are the appendix's own application of the platform's single-source-of-truth principle to its type vocabulary.

---

# The Common Definitions Schema

The shared library is a single schema whose `$defs` hold every reusable type.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema",
  "$id": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json",
  "title": "CTTP Common Definitions",
  "description": "Shared type library referenced by every CTTP v2.0 artifact schema. Owning sections cited per definition.",
  "$defs": {}
}
```

The subsections below define each member of `$defs`. Every artifact schema references these members rather than restating them.

---

# Identifier Types

Identifiers are strings constrained to fixed patterns. Each pattern is copied from the section that defines the identity format.

```json
"SchemaVersion": {
  "type": "string",
  "const": "2.0",
  "description": "Contract schema version. Fixed for this specification version."
},

"BuildId": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^[0-9]{8}-[0-9]{3}$",
  "description": "Owning build identity, e.g. '20260720-001'. Owner: Part 6 build orchestrator."
},

"SceneId": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^scene-[0-9]{3}$",
  "description": "Screenplay scene identity, e.g. 'scene-004'. Owner: 3.1.3, 4.1.2."
},

"ShotId": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^scene-[0-9]{3}-shot-[0-9]{2}$",
  "description": "Globally unique shot identity, e.g. 'scene-004-shot-02'. Prefixed by its SceneId. Owner: 4.1.2 (P-423, P-424)."
},

"StoryboardId": {
  "type": "string",
  "minLength": 1,
  "description": "Storyboard identity; matches shot-list.storyboard_id. Owner: 4.1.6, 5.1.4."
},

"RefId": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^[a-z0-9_]+_v[0-9]+$",
  "description": "Versioned continuity identifier, e.g. 'maya_v1', 'executive_dark_v1', 'operations_center_night_v1'. Owner: 4.1.7 (P-528)."
},

"ApprovalRef": {
  "type": "string",
  "minLength": 1,
  "description": "Reference to a passed upstream Quality Gate approval. Owner: 1.4.1, 5.1.4."
}
```

Identifier patterns are exact. `ShotId` encodes the `scene-NNN-shot-NN` format of 4.1.2, and every schema that carries a shot identity references `ShotId` rather than restating the pattern.

---

# Fixity & Time Types

Content hashes and timestamps recur across every sealed artifact.

```json
"ContentHash": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^sha256:[a-f0-9]{64}$",
  "description": "SHA-256 fixity over the canonical artifact body. Owner: 5.1.4, 9.1.5."
},

"CacheKey": {
  "type": "string",
  "pattern": "^sha256:[a-f0-9]{64}$",
  "description": "Deterministic content-addressed cache key. Owner: 2.1.8, 3.1.9, 4.1.13."
},

"Iso8601": {
  "type": "string",
  "format": "date-time",
  "description": "RFC 3339 / ISO-8601 timestamp. Owner: 5.1.4."
},

"DurationSeconds": {
  "type": "number",
  "exclusiveMinimum": 0,
  "description": "A positive duration in seconds."
},

"Ratio": {
  "type": "number",
  "minimum": 0,
  "maximum": 1,
  "description": "A fraction in the closed interval [0, 1]."
},

"Score": {
  "type": "number",
  "minimum": 0,
  "maximum": 1,
  "description": "A normalized quality score in [0, 1]. Owner: 2.1.7, 3.1.8."
}
```

`ContentHash` and `CacheKey` share a pattern but are distinct types because they carry distinct meaning: `ContentHash` is fixity over a body, `CacheKey` is a content address over inputs. Distinguishing them keeps each artifact's intent legible even though their lexical form is identical.

---

# Act & Enumeration Types

The three-act structure and the platform's controlled vocabularies are shared enumerations. The full vocabularies are consolidated in 9.8; the common library defines the ones referenced most widely.

```json
"Act": {
  "type": "integer",
  "enum": [1, 2, 3],
  "description": "Act in the three-act structure. Owner: 1.3.3, 2.1.6."
},

"ShotType": {
  "type": "string",
  "enum": [
    "establishing", "wide", "medium", "medium_close_up", "close_up",
    "extreme_close_up", "over_shoulder", "point_of_view", "insert",
    "tracking", "static"
  ],
  "description": "Closed shot-type vocabulary. 'random' is explicitly excluded. Owner: 4.1.3 (P-441, P-442)."
},

"RenderStrategy": {
  "type": "string",
  "enum": [
    "runway_video", "animated_still", "motion_graphics",
    "title_card", "svg_animation", "cached_clip"
  ],
  "description": "Closed render-strategy set. Exactly one per shot. Owner: 4.1.9 (P-561, P-562)."
},

"BuildType": {
  "type": "string",
  "enum": ["preview", "final"],
  "description": "Build profile. Owner: 1.3.6, 6.1.7."
}
```

Each enumeration `$def` records its owning section. A schema that constrains a shot type references `ShotType`; it never re-lists the eleven values, so the eleven values cannot diverge between schemas.

---

# The Envelope Reference

The provenance envelope (defined in full in 9.1.4) is itself a shared `$def`, so every sealed artifact composes it by reference.

```json
"ArtifactEnvelope": {
  "type": "object",
  "description": "Common provenance fields carried by every sealed artifact. See 9.1.4.",
  "properties": {
    "schema_version": { "$ref": "#/$defs/SchemaVersion" },
    "build_id":       { "$ref": "#/$defs/BuildId" },
    "approved":       { "type": "boolean" },
    "approval_ref":   { "$ref": "#/$defs/ApprovalRef" },
    "generated_at":   { "$ref": "#/$defs/Iso8601" },
    "content_hash":   { "$ref": "#/$defs/ContentHash" }
  },
  "required": ["schema_version", "build_id", "generated_at", "content_hash"]
}
```

---

# Shared Type Invariants

* INV-9.1.3-1 — Every reusable type is defined exactly once in `common/defs.schema.json`.
* INV-9.1.3-2 — Every identifier pattern is copied verbatim from its owning section.
* INV-9.1.3-3 — `ContentHash` and `CacheKey` are distinct types despite a shared lexical form.
* INV-9.1.3-4 — Every artifact schema references shared types by `$ref`, never by restatement.
* INV-9.1.3-5 — Every shared `$def` records its owning section in its `description`.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.3 is complete when:

* The common definitions schema is defined at a single well-known `$id`.
* Identifier types (`BuildId`, `SceneId`, `ShotId`, `StoryboardId`, `RefId`, `ApprovalRef`) are defined with exact patterns traced to their owning sections.
* Fixity and time types (`ContentHash`, `CacheKey`, `Iso8601`, `DurationSeconds`, `Ratio`, `Score`) are defined.
* Widely shared enumerations (`Act`, `ShotType`, `RenderStrategy`, `BuildType`) are defined and traced.
* The `ArtifactEnvelope` is defined as a shared, composable `$def`.
* Every shared type records its owning section.

---

# 9.1.4 Artifact Envelope & Provenance

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **artifact envelope**: the common set of provenance fields that every sealed artifact in the pipeline carries.

Parts 2 through 6 repeatedly attach the same provenance to their artifacts — a schema version, an owning build, an approval flag and reference, a generation timestamp, and a content hash. Part 5 makes this explicit for the rendering contracts (5.1.4); the same envelope generalizes to every sealed artifact in the platform.

Defining the envelope once means every artifact declares its provenance identically, and every validator checks provenance identically.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **Every sealed artifact declares where it came from, what it is, and whether it was approved.**

An artifact with no provenance cannot be cached deterministically, cannot be traced to an approval, and cannot be verified for integrity. The envelope makes provenance a structural property of every artifact rather than an out-of-band convention. An artifact that omits its envelope is malformed regardless of the correctness of its body.

---

# The Envelope Fields

Every sealed artifact carries the following fields.

| Field | Type | Required | Meaning |
| ----- | ---- | -------- | ------- |
| `schema_version` | `SchemaVersion` | Yes | The contract schema version the artifact conforms to. |
| `build_id` | `BuildId` | Yes | The owning build identity. |
| `approved` | boolean | Conditional | Whether the artifact passed its approval gate. Required on artifacts that cross an approval barrier. |
| `approval_ref` | `ApprovalRef` | Conditional | Reference to the passed Quality Gate; required when `approved` is present and `true`. |
| `generated_at` | `Iso8601` | Yes | The producer's generation timestamp. |
| `content_hash` | `ContentHash` | Yes | SHA-256 fixity over the canonical artifact body. |

The four always-required fields — `schema_version`, `build_id`, `generated_at`, `content_hash` — establish identity, provenance, and integrity. The two approval fields are required only on artifacts that pass an approval barrier (1.4.1), such as `shot-list.json` and `storyboard.json` on ingest to rendering (5.1.4).

---

# The Envelope Schema

The envelope is composed into an artifact with `allOf` and a local body.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema",
  "$id": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/envelope-example.schema.json",
  "type": "object",
  "allOf": [
    { "$ref": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json#/$defs/ArtifactEnvelope" }
  ],
  "properties": {
    "schema_version": true,
    "build_id": true,
    "approved": true,
    "approval_ref": true,
    "generated_at": true,
    "content_hash": true,
    "body": { "type": "object" }
  },
  "required": ["body"],
  "unevaluatedProperties": false
}
```

Artifact schemas that carry an envelope declare their envelope fields (referencing the shared `ArtifactEnvelope`) alongside their body fields, and set `unevaluatedProperties: false` so that composition does not open the object.

---

# The Approval Barrier Rule

The two approval fields express the two-stage human approval of 1.4.1.

An artifact that crosses an approval barrier — from planning into rendering, or from rendering into packaging — must carry `approved: true` and a resolvable `approval_ref`. This is the structural expression of the fail-closed approval rule (INV-1.4.1-4): an artifact presented to a downstream consumer without a resolved approval is treated as unapproved and rejected.

```text
Producer seals artifact
        │  schema_version, build_id, generated_at, content_hash
        ▼
Approval barrier (1.4.1)
        │  approved = true, approval_ref resolves
        ▼
Downstream consumer accepts
```

An artifact whose `approved` is `false` or absent at a barrier fails ingest, consistent with 5.1.4's validation-on-ingest.

---

# Fixity Rule

`content_hash` is fixity over the **canonical body**, not over the envelope.

The hash is computed over the artifact's body in canonical form (stable key ordering, normalized whitespace) and excludes the envelope's own `content_hash` field. On ingest, a consumer recomputes the hash over the canonical body and rejects the artifact if it does not match, consistent with the `content_hash` validation of 5.1.4.

This makes tampering and truncation detectable at the boundary, and it ties directly to the determinism boundary: two artifacts with identical canonical bodies have identical `content_hash` values.

---

# Envelope Invariants

* INV-9.1.4-1 — Every sealed artifact carries `schema_version`, `build_id`, `generated_at`, and `content_hash`.
* INV-9.1.4-2 — An artifact crossing an approval barrier carries `approved: true` and a resolvable `approval_ref`.
* INV-9.1.4-3 — `content_hash` is SHA-256 fixity over the canonical body, excluding the hash field itself.
* INV-9.1.4-4 — An artifact with an absent or false approval at a barrier is rejected.
* INV-9.1.4-5 — The envelope is composed by reference to `ArtifactEnvelope`, never restated.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.4 is complete when:

* The envelope fields are defined with types, requiredness, and meaning.
* The always-required and conditional (approval) fields are distinguished.
* The envelope schema and its composition via `allOf`/`unevaluatedProperties` are specified.
* The approval-barrier rule is tied to 1.4.1 and 5.1.4.
* The fixity rule for `content_hash` over the canonical body is defined.
* Envelope invariants are enumerated and enforceable.

---

# 9.1.5 Determinism, Immutability & Validation Rules

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the rules that govern how schemas are validated and how validated artifacts behave: canonicalization, validation timing, failure semantics, immutability, and versioning.

These rules are the appendix's expression of platform-wide invariants — determinism (AR3, 1.4.2), immutable planning (AR4, 1.4.2), and fail-closed behavior (AR6, 1.4.2) — applied to the artifacts the appendix validates.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **Validation is a gate, not a filter. A document passes whole or is rejected whole.**

A validator never repairs, coerces, defaults, or partially accepts an artifact. It renders a single verdict. This mirrors the fail-closed discipline of every Quality Gate in the platform: a missing value is a failure, not a default (4.1.12).

---

# Canonicalization

Determinism requires a canonical serialization.

Before hashing or comparison, an artifact body is canonicalized:

* object keys are sorted lexicographically;
* insignificant whitespace is removed;
* numbers are represented in a single canonical form;
* string encoding is UTF-8 without a byte-order mark.

Two artifacts are identical if and only if their canonical bodies are byte-identical. This is the precondition for the deterministic `content_hash` (9.1.4) and for every cache key across the platform (2.1.8, 3.1.9, 4.1.13).

---

# Validation Timing

An artifact is validated at two moments.

```text
Producer emits artifact
        │
        ▼
Validate on emit   (producer confirms its own output conforms)
        │
        ▼
Cross layer boundary
        │
        ▼
Validate on ingest (consumer confirms the input conforms)
```

Validation on emit protects the producer from shipping a malformed artifact. Validation on ingest protects the consumer from trusting one. Both use the same Part 9 schema, so a producer and consumer can never disagree about what "valid" means. This double-validation is the structural counterpart to the closed input/output sets of 5.1.4 (RIO-301, RIO-302).

---

# Failure Semantics

A validation failure is terminal for the artifact.

```text
Schema validation = PASS  →  artifact may be trusted
Schema validation = FAIL  →  artifact rejected; returned to producer
```

There is no partial acceptance, no coercion of a wrong type, and no default substituted for a missing required field. A failed artifact is returned to its producing layer for regeneration from approved inputs, never repaired in place. This is the fail-closed rule (AR6) applied at the schema boundary.

---

# Immutability

A sealed artifact is immutable.

Once an artifact is approved or emitted and sealed, its body never changes. A material change in an artifact's inputs produces a **new** artifact — a new generation, a new `content_hash`, and, where continuity identifiers are involved, a new versioned `RefId` (4.1.7) — never an in-place edit.

This is the direct application of Immutable Planning (AR4, 1.4.2) and the artifact-immutability boundaries of 2.1.8, 3.1.7, and 4.1.1 to the appendix's artifacts.

---

# Versioning

Schemas are versioned with the specification.

* A schema's `$id` is fixed within specification version `v2.0`.
* A backward-compatible refinement (adding an optional field, tightening a pattern that no valid artifact violated) may be made within `v2.0`.
* A breaking change (removing or renaming a field, changing a type, adding a required field) requires a new specification version and a new `$id` namespace segment.

Silence never revises a schema, consistent with the ADR governance of 1.4.3: a schema is binding until a later, explicitly versioned schema supersedes it.

---

# Validation Rule Invariants

* INV-9.1.5-1 — Artifacts are canonicalized before hashing or comparison.
* INV-9.1.5-2 — Every artifact is validated on emit and on ingest against the same Part 9 schema.
* INV-9.1.5-3 — Validation is fail-closed: a document passes whole or is rejected whole.
* INV-9.1.5-4 — A validator never repairs, coerces, or defaults an artifact.
* INV-9.1.5-5 — A sealed artifact is immutable; changes produce new artifacts, never in-place edits.
* INV-9.1.5-6 — A breaking schema change requires a new specification version.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.5 is complete when:

* Canonicalization is defined as the precondition for hashing and comparison.
* Validation timing on emit and on ingest is established.
* Fail-closed failure semantics with no repair, coercion, or defaulting are defined.
* Immutability is tied to AR4 and the upstream artifact-immutability boundaries.
* Schema versioning and supersession rules are defined.
* Validation-rule invariants are enumerated and enforceable.

---

# 9.1.6 Schema Registry & Index

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section is the **registry** of every schema in the appendix.

The registry is the single index a producer, consumer, validator, or orchestrator consults to find the governing schema for any artifact. It maps each artifact to its schema `$id`, its owning section, and the appendix chapter that specifies it.

The registry is authoritative for *which schema governs what*. If an artifact is not in the registry, it has no governing schema, and producing it is a defect.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **Every artifact the platform serializes appears exactly once in the registry.**

The registry is the appendix's completeness check. A gap in the registry is a gap in the contract: an artifact that some layer produces but no schema governs. Maintaining the registry as an exhaustive index is how the appendix guarantees total coverage of the pipeline.

---

# Registry Structure

Each registry entry records four fields.

| Field | Meaning |
| ----- | ------- |
| Artifact | The serialized artifact or embedded object name |
| Schema `$id` (leaf) | The kebab-case leaf of the schema `$id` under its layer segment |
| Owning Section | The Part 1–6 section that defines the artifact |
| Appendix Chapter | The Part 9 chapter that specifies the schema |

The full `$id` of any entry is `https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/<layer>/<leaf>.schema.json`.

---

# The Schema Registry

## Common (9.1)

| Artifact | Schema `$id` (leaf) | Owning Section | Appendix Chapter |
| -------- | ------------------- | -------------- | ---------------- |
| Common definitions | `common/defs` | 9.1.3 | 9.1.3 |
| Artifact envelope | `common/artifact-envelope` | 9.1.4 | 9.1.4 |

| Artifact | Schema `$id` (leaf) | Owning Section | Appendix Chapter |
| -------- | ------------------- | -------------- | ---------------- |
| Product contract | `vision/product-contract` | 1.1.1 | 9.2 |
| Layer contract | `vision/layer-contract` | 1.3.3 | 9.2 |

# Registry Invariants

* INV-9.1.6-2 — Every registry entry resolves to a schema `$id` under the `cttp/v2.0` namespace.
* INV-9.1.6-3 — Every registry entry cites an owning section.
* INV-9.1.6-4 — An artifact absent from the registry has no governing schema and may not be produced.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.1.6 is complete when:

* The registry structure (artifact, schema `$id`, owning section, appendix chapter) is defined.
* Every artifact across the six layers is listed exactly once.
* Every entry resolves to a namespaced schema `$id` and an owning section.
* The registry is established as the authoritative index of which schema governs which artifact.
* Registry invariants are enumerated and enforceable.
