| `transitions` | array | Yes | Append-only audit trail. |
| `transitions[].previous_state` / `.new_state` | `LifecycleState` | Yes | Endpoints of a transition. |
| `transitions[].timestamp` | `Iso8601` | Yes | When the transition occurred. |
| `transitions[].approval_ref` | `ApprovalRef` | No | Approval evidence for gated transitions. |

---

# Constraints & Invariants

- **INV-9.7.6-1** — Exactly one `state` is active at a time; implicit state is prohibited (Owner: 6.1.11).
- **INV-9.7.6-2** — Transitions are monotonic along `CREATED → VALIDATED → APPROVED → REFERENCED → ARCHIVED → EXPIRED → DELETED`; backward transitions are prohibited. Each `transitions[].new_state` must not precede its `previous_state` in that order.
- **INV-9.7.6-3** — `transitions_logged` is fixed `true`; every transition is auditable and persisted — no transition exists only in memory (Owner: 6.1.11).
- **INV-9.7.6-4** — `REFERENCED` artifacts are protected from deletion; `DELETED` is terminal and irreversible (payload removed, metadata retained).
- **INV-9.7.6-5** — Each artifact class has exactly one transition owner (ownership is exclusive; Owner: 6.1.11).

---

# Example

```json
{
  "schema_version": "2.0.0",
  "artifact_ref": "sha256:11a...ff",
  "build_id": "20260720-001",
  "state": "REFERENCED",
  "owner": "Build Orchestrator",
  "transitions_logged": true,
  "transitions": [
    { "previous_state": "CREATED", "new_state": "VALIDATED", "timestamp": "2026-07-20T09:20:00Z" },
    { "previous_state": "VALIDATED", "new_state": "APPROVED", "timestamp": "2026-07-20T09:22:00Z", "approval_ref": "appr-2026-0720-77" },
    { "previous_state": "APPROVED", "new_state": "REFERENCED", "timestamp": "2026-07-20T09:25:00Z" }
  ]
}
```

---

# Acceptance Criteria

- A conforming record declares a single current state from the seven canonical values.
- `transitions_logged` is `true` and the transition array is present and append-only.
- Every logged transition moves forward in canonical order; backward moves are rejected.
- Gated transitions (e.g. to `APPROVED`) may carry an `approval_ref`.

---

# 9.7.7 quality-gate-registry (`quality-gate-registry.schema.json`)

### Consolidated registry of platform Quality Gates (Owner: 6.1.6)

---

# Purpose

Quality Gates are the platform's mandatory acceptance checkpoints. Section 6.1.6 makes their passage a release requirement and states that quality takes precedence over performance in all optimization decisions (ADR-617); optimization never bypasses Quality Gates. This schema is a single registry consolidating the gates across the platform — the Story, Screenplay, Shot, and Storyboard Quality Gates, the Rendering (technical/editorial) gates, and the two human approvals (execution approval before high-cost rendering, and publish approval). Each gate is **blocking** and **fail-closed**: the Orchestrator may not override a failed mandatory gate.

---

# Canonical Schema

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema",
  "$id": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/build/quality-gate-registry.schema.json",
  "title": "QualityGateRegistry",
  "description": "Consolidated registry of platform Quality Gates. Owner: 6.1.6.",
  "type": "object",
  "additionalProperties": false,
  "required": ["schema_version", "gates"],
  "properties": {
    "schema_version": {
      "$ref": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json#/$defs/SchemaVersion"
    },
    "gates": {
      "type": "array",
      "minItems": 1,
      "items": { "$ref": "#/$defs/QualityGate" }
    }
  },
  "$defs": {
    "QualityGate": {
      "type": "object",
      "additionalProperties": false,
      "required": ["gate_id", "stage", "blocking", "fail_closed", "owning_section"],
      "properties": {
        "gate_id": {
          "type": "string",
          "description": "Stable identifier of the gate.",
          "enum": [
            "story_quality_gate",
            "screenplay_quality_gate",
            "shot_quality_gate",
            "storyboard_quality_gate",
            "rendering_technical_gate",
            "rendering_editorial_gate",
            "execution_approval",
            "publish_approval"
          ]
        },
        "stage": {
          "type": "string",
          "description": "Pipeline stage the gate guards.",
          "enum": [
            "story",
            "screenplay",
            "shot_planning",
            "storyboard",
            "rendering",
            "validation",
            "approval",
            "publication"
          ]
        },
        "gate_type": {
          "type": "string",
          "enum": ["automated", "human_approval"]
        },
        "blocking": {
          "const": true,
          "description": "Gate blocks progression on failure. Owner: 6.1.6."
        },
        "fail_closed": {
          "const": true,
          "description": "Gate denies by default; it cannot be bypassed. Owner: 6.1.6."
        },
        "owning_section": {
          "type": "string",
          "description": "Specification section that owns the gate.",
          "pattern": "^[0-9]+(\\.[0-9]+)*$"
        },
        "approval_ref": {
          "$ref": "https://schemas.insynergy.co/cttp/v2.0/common/defs.schema.json#/$defs/ApprovalRef",
          "description": "Approval evidence for human-approval gates."
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

---

# Field Reference

| Field | Type | Required | Description |
| ----- | ---- | -------- | ----------- |
| `schema_version` | `SchemaVersion` | Yes | Schema version of the registry. |
| `gates` | array of `QualityGate` | Yes | Registered gates (≥ 1). |
| `gates[].gate_id` | enum | Yes | Stable gate identifier. |
| `gates[].stage` | enum | Yes | Pipeline stage guarded. |
| `gates[].gate_type` | enum | No | Automated vs human approval. |
| `gates[].blocking` | `true` | Yes | Blocks progression on failure. |
| `gates[].fail_closed` | `true` | Yes | Denies by default; non-bypassable. |
| `gates[].owning_section` | string | Yes | Owning spec section (dotted). |
| `gates[].approval_ref` | `ApprovalRef` | No | Approval evidence for human gates. |

---

# Constraints & Invariants

- **INV-9.7.7-1** — Every gate is `blocking: true` and `fail_closed: true`; a failed mandatory gate blocks build-state progression and cannot be overridden by the Orchestrator (Owner: 6.1.6, ADR-617).
- **INV-9.7.7-2** — Optimization never bypasses Quality Gates; incremental reuse preserves gate compliance (Owner: 6.1.6 / 6.2).
- **INV-9.7.7-3** — `execution_approval` gates the `PLANNED → EXECUTING` transition, deferring high-cost rendering until approval (Principle 12, *Human Approval Before High-Cost Work*); `publish_approval` gates `READY → PUBLISHED` (Owner: 6.1.11).
- **INV-9.7.7-4** — Human-approval gates (`gate_type: "human_approval"`) must supply an `approval_ref` when satisfied; the approval event joins the audit trail.
- **INV-9.7.7-5** — `gate_id` values are unique within the registry; `owning_section` is a dotted specification reference.

---

# Example

```json
{
  "schema_version": "2.0.0",
  "gates": [
    { "gate_id": "story_quality_gate", "stage": "story", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "2.0" },
    { "gate_id": "screenplay_quality_gate", "stage": "screenplay", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "3.0" },
    { "gate_id": "shot_quality_gate", "stage": "shot_planning", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "4.0" },
    { "gate_id": "storyboard_quality_gate", "stage": "storyboard", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "4.0" },
    { "gate_id": "rendering_technical_gate", "stage": "validation", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "5.0" },
    { "gate_id": "rendering_editorial_gate", "stage": "validation", "gate_type": "automated", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "5.0" },
    { "gate_id": "execution_approval", "stage": "approval", "gate_type": "human_approval", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "6.1.11", "approval_ref": "appr-2026-0720-42" },
    { "gate_id": "publish_approval", "stage": "publication", "gate_type": "human_approval", "blocking": true, "fail_closed": true, "owning_section": "6.1.11", "approval_ref": "appr-2026-0720-99" }
  ]
}
```

---

# Acceptance Criteria

- A conforming registry lists at least one gate; every gate is blocking and fail-closed.
- The four creative gates, two rendering gates, and two human approvals are representable via the `gate_id` enumeration.
- Human-approval gates carry an `approval_ref` when satisfied.
- `gate_id` values are unique and each cites an `owning_section`.

---
# 9.8 Enumerations & Controlled Vocabularies

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section consolidates every **controlled vocabulary** in the platform into a single authoritative reference.

Enumerations are scattered across Parts 1 through 6, each defined where the concept it constrains is introduced. A validator, a reviewer, or a downstream engine that needs the complete set of shot types, render strategies, or scene purposes should not have to search six parts to assemble it. This section gathers every closed vocabulary in one place, records its exact values, and cites the section that owns each one.

The vocabularies here are the same values referenced by the schemas of 9.2 through 9.7 and by the common `$defs` of 9.1.3. This section is the human-readable index of those values; the machine-readable form is the `enum` in each schema.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **A closed vocabulary is closed everywhere or it is closed nowhere.**

An enumeration that admits eleven values in one schema and twelve in another is not a controlled vocabulary; it is two vocabularies wearing one name. Consolidating every enumeration here, with a single owning section per vocabulary, guarantees that a value added, removed, or renamed is changed in exactly one place and propagates identically to every schema that references it.

A value in this section is recorded **verbatim** — the exact case, spelling, and underscores of its owning section — consistent with Invariant P-445 (4.1.3): the platform never aliases, abbreviates, pluralizes, or re-cases an enumeration value.

---

# Structural Vocabularies

These vocabularies constrain the shape of the pipeline itself.

| Vocabulary | Values | Owner |
| ---------- | ------ | ----- |
| `layer_id` | `1`–`8` (Knowledge, Narrative, Screenplay, Direction, Rendering, Composition, Validation, Publishing) | 1.3.3 |
| `payload_type` | `structured_article_model`, `extracted_argument`, `dramatic_premise`, `developed_story`, `three_act_model`, `screenplay`, `shot_plan`, `render_routing`, `visual_assets`, `master_video`, `validated_build`, `approved_build` | 1.3.2 |
| `asset_class` | `runway_video`, `animated_still`, `motion_graphics`, `typography`, `narration` | 1.3.6 |
| `build_type` | `preview`, `final` | 1.3.6, 6.1.7 |
| `act` | `1`, `2`, `3` | 1.3.3, 2.1.6 |

---

# Story Vocabularies (Part 2)

| Vocabulary | Values | Owner |
| ---------- | ------ | ----- |
| `claim_class` | `Factual`, `Structural`, `Tension`, `Consequence` | 2.1.2 |
| `story_arc_stage` | `Normal World`, `Incident`, `Escalation`, `Crisis`, `Decision`, `Resolution` | 2.1.6 |
| `conflict_layer` | `external`, `internal`, `institutional` | 2.1.5 |
| `stake_type` | `financial_loss`, `legal_exposure`, `operational_failure`, `reputational_damage`, `institutional_collapse` | 2.1.5 |
| `story_gate_item` | `protagonist_exists`, `goal_exists`, `conflict_exists`, `stakes_exist`, `time_pressure_exists`, `decision_exists`, `resolution_exists` | 2.1.7 |
| `forbidden_story_category` | `article_summary`, `educational_lecture`, `concept_list`, `talking_heads`, `slideshow_narrative`, `narrator_only`, `decision_less` | 2.1.7 |

---

# Screenplay Vocabularies (Part 3)

| Vocabulary | Values | Owner |
| ---------- | ------ | ----- |
| `scene_purpose` (allowed) | `Introduce protagonist`, `Reveal hidden risk`, `Increase urgency`, `Create reversal`, `Force decision`, `Resolve conflict` | 3.1.3 |
| `scene_purpose` (forbidden) | `Explain concept`, `Show architecture`, `Describe framework` | 3.1.3 |
| `interior_exterior` | `INT`, `EXT`, `INT./EXT.` | 3.1.3 |
| `scene_conflict` | `Human vs Machine`, `Human vs Institution`, `Human vs Time`, `Human vs Self`, `Institution vs Reality` | 3.1.4 |
| `dialogue_category` | `Question`, `Demand`, `Refusal`, `Warning`, `Decision`, `Revelation` | 3.1.5 |
| `transition` (allowed) | `Hard Cut`, `Fade`, `Match Cut`, `L Cut`, `J Cut` | 3.1.6 |
| `transition` (forbidden) | `Page Turn`, `Spin`, `Flash`, `Explosion Transition`, `Swipe` | 3.1.6 |
| `continuity_dimension` | `Character`, `Wardrobe`, `Location`, `Time`, `Emotion`, `Countdown`, `Props` | 3.1.8 |
| `screenplay_state` | `Pending`, `Generating`, `Generated`, `Validating`, `Validated`, `AwaitingApproval`, `Approved`, `Exported`, `Failed` | 3.1.11 |
| `scene_state` | `Drafted`, `Populated`, `Validated`, `Locked` | 3.1.11 |

---

# Shot & Storyboard Vocabularies (Part 4)

| Vocabulary | Values | Owner |
| ---------- | ------ | ----- |
| `shot_type` | `establishing`, `wide`, `medium`, `medium_close_up`, `close_up`, `extreme_close_up`, `over_shoulder`, `point_of_view`, `insert`, `tracking`, `static` | 4.1.3 |
| `shot_type` (forbidden) | `random` | 4.1.3 |
| `lens` | `24mm`, `35mm`, `50mm`, `85mm` | 4.1.4 |
| `angle` | `eye`, `low`, `high` | 4.1.4 |
| `movement` | `static`, `slow_push`, `slow_pull`, `dolly`, `pan`, `tilt` | 4.1.4 |
| `speed` | `slow` | 4.1.4 |
| `composition` | `rule_of_thirds` (controlled vocabulary; extended per Character/Location bibles) | 4.1.6 |
| `lighting` | `low_key` (controlled) | 4.1.6 |
| `palette` | `graphite` (controlled) | 4.1.6 |
| `depth` | `deep_focus` (controlled) | 4.1.6 |
| `render_strategy` | `runway_video`, `animated_still`, `motion_graphics`, `title_card`, `svg_animation`, `cached_clip` | 4.1.9 |
| `runway_eligible_characteristic` | `facial reaction`, `reaching movement`, `walking`, `camera movement`, `dramatic reveal` | 4.1.9 |
| `runway_ineligible_characteristic` | `diagrams`, `countdowns`, `typography`, `UI`, `static environment` | 4.1.9 |
| `shot_gate_check` | `purpose_exists`, `camera_defined`, `blocking_defined`, `emotion_defined`, `continuity_valid`, `render_strategy_defined`, `single_action`, `single_camera_move` | 4.1.12 |
| `storyboard_gate_check` | `composition`, `continuity`, `pacing`, `render_balance`, `concept_ratio`, `emotional_rhythm` | 4.1.12 |

The frame vocabularies (`composition`, `lighting`, `palette`, `depth`) are controlled but extensible through the Character and Location Bibles: the canonical values (`rule_of_thirds`, `low_key`, `graphite`, `deep_focus`) are the reference set, and additional values are admitted only when defined in a bible. A frame value is never free prose.

---

# Rendering & Build Vocabularies (Parts 5–6)

| Vocabulary | Values | Owner |
| ---------- | ------ | ----- |
| `render_task_state` | as defined by the render task state machine | 5.4.3 |
| `failure_class` | as defined by the failure-classification policy | 5.4.5 |
| `rendering_profile` | `preview`, `final` (production) | 5.6.4, 5.6.5 |
| `operational_artifact_state` | `CREATED`, `VALIDATED`, `APPROVED`, `REFERENCED`, `ARCHIVED`, `EXPIRED`, `DELETED` | 6.1.11 |
| `approval_gate` | `story_approval`, `final_approval` | 1.4.1 |
| `approval_outcome` | `approved`, `rejected`, `absent` | 1.4.1 |

The rendering task-state and failure-class vocabularies are owned by their Part 5 state-machine and failure-classification sections respectively; the schemas of 9.6 record their exact members. This table lists the vocabularies; the render-task and retry-policy schemas (9.6.5, 9.6.7) hold their authoritative `enum` values.

---

# Enumeration Invariants

* INV-9.8-1 — Every controlled vocabulary in the platform appears in this section with its owning section.
* INV-9.8-2 — Every value is recorded verbatim, preserving case and underscores.
* INV-9.8-3 — A vocabulary has exactly one owning section; schemas reference it, never redefine it.
* INV-9.8-4 — `random` is excluded from `shot_type`; `absent` approval is treated as `rejected`.
* INV-9.8-5 — Frame vocabularies are controlled and extended only through the Character and Location Bibles.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.8 is complete when:

* Every closed vocabulary across Parts 1–6 is consolidated with its exact values.
* Each vocabulary cites exactly one owning section.
* Allowed and forbidden value sets are distinguished where the owning section forbids specific values.
* The values match the `enum` members of the schemas in 9.2–9.7 and the common `$defs` of 9.1.3.
* Enumeration invariants are enumerated and enforceable.

---

# 9.9 Cross-Schema Referential Integrity & Validation

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **referential integrity** rules that hold *between* artifacts, which no single-artifact schema can express.

A schema validates one document in isolation: it confirms that a `shot_id` matches its pattern, that a required field is present, that an enumeration value is legal. It cannot confirm that the `shot_id` in a camera plan actually refers to a shot that exists in the shot list, or that every shot in the shot list has exactly one storyboard frame. Those are cross-artifact properties, and they are the properties on which the pipeline's correctness ultimately depends.

This section gathers those cross-artifact rules, states them precisely, and assigns each to the validator that enforces it.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **A field that references another artifact is a promise. Referential integrity is the check that the promise is kept.**

Per-schema validation is necessary but not sufficient. A shot list of individually valid shots can still reference a location that no bible defines. A storyboard of individually valid frames can still omit a shot the shot list requires. Referential integrity is the second validation layer — applied after every artifact is individually valid — that confirms the artifacts agree with one another.

---

# Identity Resolution

Every reference resolves to an artifact that defines the referenced identity.

| Reference | Resolves Against | Rule | Owner |
| --------- | ---------------- | ---- | ----- |
| `shot.scene_id` | screenplay scenes | must reference an existing scene | 4.1.2 (P-401) |
| `shot.shot_id` prefix | `shot.scene_id` | `shot_id` is prefixed by its `scene_id` | 4.1.2 (P-424) |
| `shot.subject` | Character Bible | must resolve to a bible entry | 4.1.2, 4.1.7 (P-426) |
| `shot.location` | Location Bible | must resolve to a bible entry | 4.1.2, 4.1.7 (P-426) |
| `continuity.character`/`wardrobe`/`hairstyle` | Character Bible | each must resolve | 4.1.7 (P-523–P-525) |
| `continuity.location` | Location Bible | must resolve | 4.1.7 (P-526) |
| `storyboard.storyboard_id` | `shot-list.storyboard_id` | must be equal | 5.1.4 |
| `approval_ref` | passed Quality Gate | must resolve to a passed gate | 1.4.1, 5.1.4 |

A reference that does not resolve is a referential-integrity failure. The referencing artifact is rejected and returned for re-planning; the validator never invents the missing target (4.1.7).

---

# Bijective Coverage

Several artifacts must cover exactly the same set of shots — no missing, no extra.

```text
shot-list.shots[].shot_id
        │  (must equal, as a set)
        ├── storyboard.shots[].shot_id        (bijective, 5.1.4)
        ├── camera-plan.shots[].shot_id       (complete coverage, 5.1.4)
        └── render-strategy.shots[].shot_id   (one entry per shot, 5.1.4)
```

The rule is exact-set-equality, not containment. The set of `shot_id` values in the storyboard must be **exactly equal** to the set in the shot list — every shot is storyboarded, and no storyboard frame references a shot that does not exist (5.1.4). The camera plan and render strategy must likewise cover every shot exactly once.

| Coverage Rule | Constraint | Owner |
| ------------- | ---------- | ----- |
| Storyboard ↔ shot list | bijective on `shot_id` | 5.1.4 |
| Camera plan ↔ shot list | one camera entry per shot | 5.1.4 |
| Render strategy ↔ shot list | one strategy per shot | 4.1.9, 5.1.4 |
| Render task ↔ shot | one render task per shot | 5.1.5 |

---

# Ordering & Acyclicity

Some references impose ordering or acyclicity constraints across an artifact set.

* **Total shot order.** The `(scene_index, shot_index)` pairs in the shot list form a total order with no duplicates (5.1.4).
* **Acyclic dependencies.** Every `dependencies[]` entry references a `shot_id` in the same list, and the dependency graph is acyclic (5.1.4).
* **Forward-only time.** Temporal markers across a scene's shots are monotonic; a later shot never precedes an earlier one (4.1.8, P-544).
* **Acyclic build graph.** The build dependency graph (6.1.3) is a DAG; explicit dependencies never form a cycle.

---

# Fixity & Determinism

Integrity extends to content, not only references.

* **Content hash.** Every sealed artifact's `content_hash` must equal the recomputed SHA-256 over its canonical body (9.1.4, 5.1.4).
* **Cache-key determinism.** A cache key is the SHA-256 of its exact named components; identical components yield an identical key and an identical artifact (2.1.8, 3.1.9, 4.1.13).
* **Ratio partition.** The render-strategy ratios (`runway_ratio + animated_ratio + graphics_ratio`) sum to 1.0 (4.1.13, P-643); act-duration ratios sum to 1.0 (2.1.6); the hybrid `runway_ratio` stays below its configured cap (4.1.10).

---

# The Validation Matrix

Each integrity rule is enforced by a named validator, at a named boundary.

| Integrity Rule | Enforced By | Boundary |
| -------------- | ----------- | -------- |
| Per-artifact structure | Part 9 schema validation | emit and ingest (9.1.5) |
| Character/location reference resolution | ContinuityValidator (4.1.14) | shot validation |
| Time monotonicity | ContinuityValidator (4.1.8) | shot validation |
| Bijective storyboard coverage | Rendering ingest gate (5.1.4) | rendering ingest |
| Approval resolution | Approval barrier (1.4.1) | approval barrier |
| Content-hash fixity | Consumer on ingest (5.1.4) | every ingest |
| Ratio caps and partitions | Shot/Storyboard Quality Gate (4.1.10, 4.1.12) | pre-render gate |
| Build-graph acyclicity | Build orchestrator (6.1.3) | build planning |

Referential integrity is checked **after** per-artifact schema validation and **before** the artifact set is trusted for the next stage. Both layers are fail-closed: a resolution failure or a coverage gap blocks progression exactly as a schema violation does.

---

# Referential Integrity Invariants

* INV-9.9-1 — Every reference field resolves to an artifact that defines the referenced identity.
* INV-9.9-2 — Storyboard, camera plan, and render strategy cover the shot list bijectively.
* INV-9.9-3 — Shot ordering is a total order; dependency and build graphs are acyclic; time is forward-only.
* INV-9.9-4 — Every sealed artifact's `content_hash` verifies against its canonical body.
* INV-9.9-5 — Referential integrity is validated after per-artifact structure and is fail-closed.

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section 9.9 is complete when:

* Every cross-artifact reference is listed with its resolution target and owning section.
* Bijective-coverage rules over the shot set are defined and exact.
* Ordering and acyclicity rules are enumerated.
* Fixity, cache-key determinism, and ratio-partition rules are defined.
* A validation matrix assigns each integrity rule to a validator and a boundary.
* Referential-integrity invariants are enumerated and enforceable.

---

# 9.10 Error Codes, Glossary, Index & Acceptance

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.0

---

# Purpose

This section closes Part 9. It defines the **error-code registry** a validator emits on failure, a **glossary** of appendix terms, a pointer to the consolidated **schema index**, and the **acceptance criteria** for Part 9 as a whole.

A validation failure must be actionable. An error that says only "invalid" routes the defect nowhere. The error-code registry gives every class of failure a stable code, a meaning, and the owning authority to which the defect is routed — mirroring the traceable gate reports of 4.1.12.

---

# Design Philosophy

The appendix adopts the following rule.

> **A rejection names what failed, where, and who owns the fix.**

Fail-closed validation is only useful if its failures are diagnosable. Every error code in the registry names a failure class, cites the rule it violates, and routes correction to the section that owns the rule. A rejection is a work order, not a dead end.

---

# Error-Code Registry

Validation failures are classified into stable codes.

| Code | Class | Meaning | Routed To |
| ---- | ----- | ------- | --------- |
| `E-SCHEMA-001` | Structure | A required field is absent | Producing layer |
| `E-SCHEMA-002` | Structure | A field has the wrong type | Producing layer |
| `E-SCHEMA-003` | Structure | An unexpected property is present (`additionalProperties`) | Producing layer |
| `E-SCHEMA-004` | Vocabulary | A value is outside its enumeration | Owning vocabulary section (9.8) |
| `E-SCHEMA-005` | Pattern | An identifier does not match its pattern | 9.1.3 / owning section |
| `E-REF-001` | Reference | A reference does not resolve (bible, scene, approval) | ContinuityValidator / approval barrier |
| `E-REF-002` | Coverage | Bijective coverage is broken (missing/extra shot) | Rendering ingest (5.1.4) |
| `E-REF-003` | Ordering | Shot order, dependency graph, or time is non-monotonic/cyclic | ContinuityValidator / orchestrator |
| `E-FIX-001` | Fixity | `content_hash` does not verify | Producing layer |
| `E-APPROVAL-001` | Approval | `approved` absent or false at a barrier | Human approval (1.4.1) |
| `E-RATIO-001` | Constraint | A ratio cap or partition is violated | Quality Gate (4.1.10, 4.1.12) |
| `E-IMMUT-001` | Immutability | A sealed artifact was mutated in place | Producing layer |

Every code is fail-closed: emitting it blocks the artifact and returns it to the routed authority. No code carries an override or "accept anyway" path, consistent with the gate discipline of 4.1.12 and 2.1.7.

---

# Glossary

| Term | Definition |
| ---- | ---------- |
| Artifact | A serialized document produced by one layer and consumed by another |
| Envelope | The common provenance fields (`schema_version`, `build_id`, `approved`, `approval_ref`, `generated_at`, `content_hash`) carried by every sealed artifact |
| Sealed | An artifact that has been approved or emitted and is therefore immutable |
| Canonical body | The artifact body in canonical serialization, over which `content_hash` is computed |
| Common `$defs` | The shared type library at `common/defs.schema.json` |
| Bijective coverage | Exact set-equality of `shot_id` values between artifacts |
| Referential integrity | The property that every reference resolves to a defining artifact |
| Owning section | The Part 1–6 section that defines an artifact or vocabulary |
| Fail-closed | The property that a missing or ambiguous value is a failure, never a default |
| Fixity | Integrity of an artifact body verified by `content_hash` |
| `RefId` | A versioned continuity identifier (e.g. `maya_v1`) |

---

# Schema Index

The authoritative index of every schema — artifact, `$id`, owning section, and appendix chapter — is the **Schema Registry** of Section 9.1.6. It is not duplicated here; 9.1.6 is the single source.

The appendix covers, in total:

| Chapter | Layer | Schemas |
| ------- | ----- | ------- |
| 9.1 | Common | 2 (common defs, envelope) |
| 9.2 | Vision / Architecture (Part 1) | 5 |
| 9.3 | Story Engine (Part 2) | 16 |
| 9.4 | Screenplay Engine (Part 3) | 8 |
| 9.5 | Shot Planner & Storyboard (Part 4) | 11 |
| 9.6 | Rendering Platform (Part 5) | 9 |
| 9.7 | Performance & Build (Part 6) | 7 |

The consolidated vocabularies (9.8), the referential-integrity rules (9.9), and the error-code registry (9.10) apply across every schema in the index.

---

# Part 9 Invariants

* INV-9.10-1 — Every validation failure maps to a stable error code with a routed authority.
* INV-9.10-2 — Every error code is fail-closed with no override path.
* INV-9.10-3 — The Schema Registry of 9.1.6 is the single authoritative schema index.
* INV-9.10-4 — Part 9 introduces no artifact, field, constraint, or vocabulary absent from Parts 1–6.

---

# Part 9 Acceptance Criteria

Part 9 is complete when:

* Every serialized artifact and embedded object across Parts 1–6 has exactly one governing schema in the appendix.
* Every schema is expressed in JSON Schema draft 2020-12, carries a stable namespaced `$id`, and is closed by default.
* Shared types are defined once in the common `$defs` and referenced everywhere.
* Every sealed artifact composes the provenance envelope, and the approval-barrier and fixity rules are enforced.
* Every controlled vocabulary is consolidated with its owning section and verbatim values.
* Cross-schema referential integrity — resolution, bijective coverage, ordering, acyclicity, fixity — is defined and assigned to validators.
* Determinism, immutability, and fail-closed validation rules are established and traced to their platform invariants (AR3, AR4, AR6).
* Every validation failure maps to a stable, routed error code.
* Every schema and vocabulary is traceable to an owning section, and the appendix adds nothing absent from Parts 1–6.

---

# Part 9 Closure

Part 9 has formalized the complete structural contract of the platform.

```text
9.1  → Schema Architecture & Conventions
9.2  → Vision & Architecture Layer Schemas
9.3  → Story Engine Layer Schemas
9.4  → Screenplay Engine Layer Schemas
9.5  → Shot Planner & Storyboard Layer Schemas
9.6  → Rendering Platform Layer Schemas
9.7  → Performance & Build Layer Schemas
9.8  → Enumerations & Controlled Vocabularies
9.9  → Cross-Schema Referential Integrity & Validation
9.10 → Error Codes, Glossary, Index & Acceptance
```

Every artifact the platform produces or consumes now has a machine-checkable schema, a place in the registry, a set of controlled vocabularies, a set of cross-artifact integrity rules, and a defined failure vocabulary. The appendix adds no meaning; it makes the meaning already established in Parts 1 through 6 structurally enforceable at every layer boundary.

Part 9 is complete. The Master Specification v2.0 is closed.
